    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer11089131348083640663">Miss Pettigrew, an approaching-middle-age governess, was accustomed to a household of unruly English children. When her employment agency sends her to the wrong address, her life takes an unexpected turn. The alluring nightclub singer, Delysia LaFosse, becomes her new employer, and Miss Pettigrew encounters a kind of glamour that she had only met before at the movies. Over</span>
  <span id="freeText11089131348083640663" style="display:none">Miss Pettigrew, an approaching-middle-age governess, was accustomed to a household of unruly English children. When her employment agency sends her to the wrong address, her life takes an unexpected turn. The alluring nightclub singer, Delysia LaFosse, becomes her new employer, and Miss Pettigrew encounters a kind of glamour that she had only met before at the movies. Over the course of a single day, both women are changed forever.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7266953635462104927">This sweet little cute little naughty little novel from 1938, with its nudity, its cocaine and its multiple sexual partners (all before page 20) unfortunately throws me into the old quandary which goes – what if you're in the middle of a grand evening with some of your best pals and you're as happy as Larry, whoever he was, having a great time, and then one of them out of the blue makes a racist remark?<br/>What do you do? Stop the party? Denounce your friend? Turn a lovely evening into a memorable h</span>
  <span id="freeText7266953635462104927" style="display:none">This sweet little cute little naughty little novel from 1938, with its nudity, its cocaine and its multiple sexual partners (all before page 20) unfortunately throws me into the old quandary which goes – what if you're in the middle of a grand evening with some of your best pals and you're as happy as Larry, whoever he was, having a great time, and then one of them out of the blue makes a racist remark?<br />What do you do? Stop the party? Denounce your friend? Turn a lovely evening into a memorable horror-show about which people will wince for years?<br /><br />I was motoring through this book and thinking it was kind of a British counterpart to Anita Loos' Gentlemen Prefer Blondes – well, actually, it was The Monkees to Anita Loos' Beatles, but still good fun, as The Monkees are, when Miss Pettigrew on page 162 offers some advice to Miss LaFosse, who is trying to choose between two suitors :<br /><br /><i>"Now the first one, he was kind too," said Miss Pettigrew earnestly, "but well, my dear. I wouldn't advise marrying him. I don't like to jump to conclusions but I think there was a little </i>Jew<i> in him. He wasn't quite </i>English.<i> And, well, I do think when it comes to marriage it's safer to stick with your own nationality."<br />"Certainly," said Miss LaFosse, demurely. </i><br /><br />Oh yes, that came 12 pages after this – here's one of the suitors speaking :<br /><br /><i>"Now Delysia's a little devil and there's times I could flay her alive, and obviously she needs a little physical correction, but I'm the only right man to do it."</i><br /><br />So, at what point do you shrug and say well, this is before all that political correctness, so you have to – er, roll with the punches (ooh that doesn't sound right) – er, I mean you have to give them a bit of leeway, er don't you? The past is another country and all that? Well, I didn't leave the party, I finished the book, there were no embarassing scenes, but I don't think me and Winifred Watson will be meeting up again any time soon.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7266953635462104927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1827009700" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1827009700" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1827009700?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11768149-miss-pettigrew-lives-for-a-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=dated-social-attitudes">dated-social-attitudes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=brain-candy">brain-candy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1827009700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer190188663369603187">3.75 stars. In this 1938 book, the proper Miss Pettigrew, a 40 year old faded and timid governess who's fallen into desperate poverty, is sent to a new job by her employment agency. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520012505i/25150567._SY540_.jpg' width='270' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The address she's given is for a sexy nightclub singer, Miss LaFosse, who's in the throes of Man Troubles: she's juggling two lovers, with a third hopefully waiting in the wings. Miss Pettigrew is scandalized but intrigued. Miss LaFosse begs Miss Pettigrew to help her out: <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520012505i/25150566.jpg' width='196' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>... and somehow Miss Pettigrew rises to the </span>
  <span id="freeText190188663369603187" style="display:none">3.75 stars. In this 1938 book, the proper Miss Pettigrew, a 40 year old faded and timid governess who's fallen into desperate poverty, is sent to a new job by her employment agency. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520012505i/25150567._SY540_.jpg" width="270" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The address she's given is for a sexy nightclub singer, Miss LaFosse, who's in the throes of Man Troubles: she's juggling two lovers, with a third hopefully waiting in the wings. Miss Pettigrew is scandalized but intrigued. Miss LaFosse begs Miss Pettigrew to help her out: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520012505i/25150566.jpg" width="196" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>... and somehow Miss Pettigrew rises to the occasion. A friendship starts to form, and one thing leads to another in the most crazy, wonderful day the downtrodden Miss Pettigrew has ever experienced in her life.<br><br>In so many ways this novel is delightful, fluffy fun, with a delicious sense of humor. It's wonderful to see Miss Pettigrew start to blossom, Cinderella-like; even a makeover is included in the fun:<blockquote> Miss Pettigrew, rapt, thrilled, transported, gazed at herself as her dreams had painted her. A lump came into her throat. Her eyes became misty. <br><br>‘Guinevere,’ screamed Miss Dubarry in a panic. ‘For God’s sake, control yourself.’ <br><br>‘Guinevere,’ gasped Miss LaFosse. ‘Control, I implore you. Your make-up. Remember your duty to your make-up.’<br><br>Miss Pettigrew made a valiant effort. ‘Most certainly,’ said Miss Pettigrew with dignity. 'England expects!'</blockquote>Unfortunately, the occasional, casual racism (against Italians in particular - the word "dago" is used) and anti-Semitism (this guy looks like he has Jewish blood! Oh noes!!) left a bad taste in my mouth. I give older books somewhat of a pass on being dated and non-PC, but I'm still shaking my head over the wholehearted embrace of racist ideas by our heroine. (Whether the author agreed with Miss Pettigrew is, I suppose, up for debate. See the thread for discussion.) A lot of readers are able to handwave this kind of thing in an older book, and it's occasional here (maybe 6 or 8 different passages in the book), but be advised. If you're going to be deeply offended by this sort of thing, or by things like a man physically trying to shake some sense into the woman he loves, you should probably give this a hard pass.<br><br>Miss Pettigrew, like Valancy in L.M. Montgomery's delightful <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/95693.The_Blue_Castle" title="The Blue Castle by L.M. Montgomery" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blue Castle</a>, is a dispirited, bullied woman ready to start breaking society's rules. The company Miss Pettigrew starts keeping lives a fast lifestyle, but ultimately the story affirms friendship and old-fashioned values, which I wouldn't have expected initially.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520013093i/25150679._SY540_.jpg" width="360" height="480" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Kindle version of this novel (which is far too expensive for an 80 year old novel) does have the original illustrations, which are delightful. On the down side, it desperately needs another round of copy editing. If you have a choice, get a hard copy.<br><br>March 2018 group read with the Retro Reads group.</span>
  <a data-text-id="190188663369603187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2041657842" />
    <a title="Melindam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36434323-melindam"><img alt="Melindam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484595601p2/36434323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2041657842?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melindam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melindam" href="/user/show/36434323-melindam">Melindam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22747134-miss-pettigrew-lives-for-a-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36434323-melindam?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36434323-melindam?shelf=forgotten-classics">forgotten-classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36434323-melindam?shelf=persephone-books">persephone-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36434323-melindam?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36434323-melindam?shelf=anglophilia">anglophilia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36434323-melindam?shelf=lovely-makeover-story">lovely-makeover-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36434323-melindam?shelf=cozy-comfort-read">cozy-comfort-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041657842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9976583302741054432"><i>"She, Miss Pettigrew, spinster, maiden lady, dull nonentity, jobless, incompetent, was bound for a night club, clad in splendour: painted like the best of them, shameless as the worst of them, uplifted with ecstasy. ‘Oh!’ thought Miss Pettigrew blissfully, ‘I think I’d like to die to-night before I waken up."</i><br/><br/><b>This is Pure, Unadulterated ESCAPISM! Utter delight and bliss!</b> This book makes you feel like you are on sugar high after a deceptively light and delicious sugary cake.<br/><br/>The time is 1938, the p</span>
  <span id="freeText9976583302741054432" style="display:none"><i>"She, Miss Pettigrew, spinster, maiden lady, dull nonentity, jobless, incompetent, was bound for a night club, clad in splendour: painted like the best of them, shameless as the worst of them, uplifted with ecstasy. ‘Oh!’ thought Miss Pettigrew blissfully, ‘I think I’d like to die to-night before I waken up."</i><br /><br /><b>This is Pure, Unadulterated ESCAPISM! Utter delight and bliss!</b> This book makes you feel like you are on sugar high after a deceptively light and delicious sugary cake.<br /><br />The time is 1938, the place: London. Miss Guinevere Pettigrew, 40-year old, lonely, overlooked, dowdy spinster, sets out to find a job -her last hope before her landlady will turn her out of her lodgings - as a governess. She is given an address, where she goes and when the door is opened by the lovely, but distressed Delysia LaFosse -actress and singer in a nightclub- Miss P. finds herself in a WORLD, she's never known before: a scandalous, glittering and dangerously seductive world of the demi monde. <br /><br />Obviously, Miss LaFosse does not need a governess, but Miss Pettigrew helps her out of a tight spot <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It is paramount that she gets rid of one lover before she gets caught by another. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and earns her undying admiration in the process. Before the misunderstanding of Miss P's situation can be cleared up, further predicaments arise and Miss Pettigrew -like never before- rises up to all occasions brilliantly. She knows, of course, that she should turn her back on this world of sin and sinners, but she is totally fascinated and she just cannot.<br /><br />I don't usually draw comparison between authors, but I think this time it seems just fitting to say that Winifred Watson's writing reminds me a bit of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7963.P_G__Wodehouse" title="P.G. Wodehouse" rel="nofollow noopener">P. G. Wodehouse</a>. You get the same high &amp; light entertainment factor.<br /><br />I also encourage you to check out the movie, which is excellent with Frances McDormand &amp; Amy Adams &amp; absolutely manages to catch and reflect the spirit of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9976583302741054432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3543055664" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3543055664" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68708752-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505852430p2/68708752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3543055664?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/68708752-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68708752-beverly?shelf=comic-historical-novel">comic-historical-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3543055664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9666159523377209687">She certainly does! This is a fun, comic novel about a downtrodden, destitute, middle-aged governess who, while searching for work, gets caught up in a great adventure. Miss Pettigrew knocks on the door of a lovely, young woman who seems to jump from one crisis to another. Miss LaFosse is warm and kind, but not a lady, she needs help and Miss Pettigrew obliges over and over again. <br/><br/>Working with decency and common sense and a little booze thrown in, Miss Pettigrew not only lives for a day, she sei</span>
  <span id="freeText9666159523377209687" style="display:none">She certainly does! This is a fun, comic novel about a downtrodden, destitute, middle-aged governess who, while searching for work, gets caught up in a great adventure. Miss Pettigrew knocks on the door of a lovely, young woman who seems to jump from one crisis to another. Miss LaFosse is warm and kind, but not a lady, she needs help and Miss Pettigrew obliges over and over again. <br /><br />Working with decency and common sense and a little booze thrown in, Miss Pettigrew not only lives for a day, she seizes the day and saves everyone around her, herself included. The only caveat I have is an oozing blotch if anti-Semitism, or this would be perfect. I have to remind myself that it was written in 1938, but still, it is a shame that hate should blemish a sweet, silly story like this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9666159523377209687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2256273047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2256273047" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2256273047?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2256273047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer68530664609237862">Down-on-her-luck 40 year old governess Miss Guinevere Pettigrew needs to get a teaching job or she’ll be evicted. But little does she know when she stumbles into the glamorous life of socialite Miss Delysia LaFosse, her fortunes are about to change drastically - today, for the first time in her bleak existence, Miss Pettigrew will LIVE! <br/><br/>Winifred Watson’s Miss Pettigrew Lives For a Day is the embodiment of the word “pleasant”. It’s just such a nice little novel full of light, soapy romance and in</span>
  <span id="freeText68530664609237862" style="display:none">Down-on-her-luck 40 year old governess Miss Guinevere Pettigrew needs to get a teaching job or she’ll be evicted. But little does she know when she stumbles into the glamorous life of socialite Miss Delysia LaFosse, her fortunes are about to change drastically - today, for the first time in her bleak existence, Miss Pettigrew will LIVE! <br /><br />Winifred Watson’s Miss Pettigrew Lives For a Day is the embodiment of the word “pleasant”. It’s just such a nice little novel full of light, soapy romance and inoffensive people, it’s impossible to dislike! That said, it’s far from a flawless read. <br /><br />Loosely a modern(ish - the book was first published in 1938) re-imagining of Cinderella, the story takes place over the course of a single day so the pacing is brisk. In part because of that, it’s a quick read despite a vague, meandering purpose (you don’t really notice it’s a Cinderella retelling until the second half) and a lack of plot. It also oddly reads a bit like a play as most of the story takes place in a single room everyone walks in and out of - though maybe that was just the style of rom-coms back then? <br /><br />The characters are unoriginal sketches - conventional upper-class Londoners who enjoy their booze, drugs (given the otherwise discreet atmosphere of the book, cocaine makes a slightly jarring appearance in an early scene!) and late nights while Miss Pettigrew is almost a caricature of humility - but they’re mostly likeable, and, while I’m not a huge romance fan, the cast’s relationship intrigues and playful tone were amusing enough. That said, I’m not sure what exactly Miss Pettigrew does that impresses everyone to give her the status she acquires throughout but I’m putting that down to being one of the dated features of the time (along with a couple of distasteful and disturbingly casual anti-Semitic slurs she makes). <br /><br />Aside from the dull grey cover, I liked the book’s presentation a lot which strongly evoked the era. Contemporary illustrations are dotted throughout in a style that feels of the time and complemented the text well. The ‘30s endpaper designs are quaint and even the font looks suitably old-fashioned (ITC Baskerville - love it!). <br /><br />Though not an “important” or highly distinguishable novel, I’m glad that Persephone Books rescued Miss Pettigrew Lives For a Day from an obscurity it doesn’t deserve. And, while it’s not the most memorable or exciting story, it is well-written, entertaining for a period piece and, above all, charming. If you’re after a perfectly accessible, amiable read with a feel-good ending, you could do worse than this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="68530664609237862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MsAprilVincent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MsAprilVincent" href="/user/show/600502-msaprilvincent">MsAprilVincent</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906462024" href="/book/show/2277185.Miss_Pettigrew_Lives_for_a_Day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/600502-msaprilvincent?shelf=1001-books-list">1001-books-list</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18579463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14169416993135325585">I bought this book after having seen the movie and, as is so often the case, the book is much, much better than the film. While I enjoyed the movie very much, I loved this book and flew through it. <br/><br/>Miss Pettigrew has been repressed and oppressed and one day, after meeting Delysia LaFosse, throws her convictions to the wind and decides to enjoy herself. She has the best time of her life, makes tons of new friends, becomes a sort of "fixer" for Delysia and her degenerate crowd, earns the admiratio</span>
  <span id="freeText14169416993135325585" style="display:none">I bought this book after having seen the movie and, as is so often the case, the book is much, much better than the film. While I enjoyed the movie very much, I loved this book and flew through it. <br /><br />Miss Pettigrew has been repressed and oppressed and one day, after meeting Delysia LaFosse, throws her convictions to the wind and decides to enjoy herself. She has the best time of her life, makes tons of new friends, becomes a sort of "fixer" for Delysia and her degenerate crowd, earns the admiration of a host of young people, and possibly finds a little romance of her own ... all in the course of 24 hours. <br /><br />The subject matter seems a tiny bit racy, particularly when one takes into account that this was written by a woman in the early 20th century, when the Hays Code would have had us believe that nobody drank alcohol, had sex, or said dirty words, when men were valiant and heroic, and women were faithful and timid and believed they were "the weaker sex." That's all shot to hell here, and rightly so.<br /><br />I love books about heroines who decide to just go for it, to toss away inhibitions and societal restrictions, who learn that the rules they've followed for years are arbitrary and often misogynistic, and who "find themselves" when they'd thought their lives were over. <br /><br />This is a short, charming read, and I smiled the entire time I was reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14169416993135325585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_403736038" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/403736038" />

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906462024" href="/book/show/2277185.Miss_Pettigrew_Lives_for_a_Day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=r2016">r2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=r2018">r2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=c20th">c20th</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=r2020">r2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=literary">literary</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer403736038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7453790784206256591">Comfort re-read :0)<br/><br/><i>“How do we know what latent possibilities of achievements we possess?</i><br/><br/>It is always with a little trepidation that I re-visit a book I loved so much. Will it still be a favourite or will it have lost something in the intervening years? I remember enjoying this novel so much back in 2008 and kept fond memories.<br/><br/>So, how was it? The answer - I devoured it in one evening, giggling a few times here and there. I'd forgotten the details and it was lovely to re-discover them. It is a lig</span>
  <span id="freeText7453790784206256591" style="display:none">Comfort re-read :0)<br /><br /><i>“How do we know what latent possibilities of achievements we possess?</i><br /><br />It is always with a little trepidation that I re-visit a book I loved so much. Will it still be a favourite or will it have lost something in the intervening years? I remember enjoying this novel so much back in 2008 and kept fond memories.<br /><br />So, how was it? The answer - I devoured it in one evening, giggling a few times here and there. I'd forgotten the details and it was lovely to re-discover them. It is a light read that combines vaudeville and fairy tale to great delight. Miss Pettigrew is endearing with her mixture of naivety and wisdom, and I couldn't resist following her on her day of freedom from social mores, discovering a world of brilliance and luxury totally different from her own drab existence. She finds she has a real skill at repartees, even if often unconsciously done. The scenes between her and the various characters she meets are often very funny, full of ridicule, and pure theatre.<br /><br />Through those few hours, she readjusts her moral compass to great humour. She grows in confidence, becoming someone that people can rely on and a problem-solver. She finally starts to see her worth and becomes herself. This is however a novel of its time and the 1930s had views that we find nowadays distasteful (and rightly so). I of course don't agree with the couple of racist and sexist comments made in the book but I understand their context. Should they be removed? No. I don't believe books, or films, should ever be censured. That would go against freedom of speech and would only lead us to catastrophe. How was Watson's novel regarded in her own time after all? She does describe women in a different light, more in charge of their destinies than the so-called ladies, using all they have to their advantage, which doesn't deny kindness and compassion.<br /><br />Is it still worth 5 stars? Totally. This is pure escapism. A feel-good book that will give hours of fun again and again. Thank you Persephone Books for rescuing this little gem.<br /><br />PS: What is it about the surname Pettigrew? Two of my favourite books have it in their title (the other is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6643090.Major_Pettigrew_s_Last_Stand" title="Major Pettigrew's Last Stand by Helen Simonson" rel="nofollow noopener">Major Pettigrew's Last Stand</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7453790784206256591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

And you glance at the clock, and do the math (it will take you x number of hours to read this book) and decide you’d better clear your calendar for the next day. And then a truly horrible thought leaps into your mind - that if you were a widow you would not have to stop reading this book in order to ma</span>
  <span id="freeText3385900354085299095" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420333585i/13206141.jpg" width="150" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My Favorite Book read in 2014</b><br><br>Did you ever get 15 – 20 pages into a book, and your whole body starts to quiver slightly, because it starts to dawn on you that you MAY just be reading a 5 star book? And you glance at the clock, and do the math (it will take you x number of hours to read this book) and decide you’d better clear your calendar for the next day. And then a truly horrible thought leaps into your mind - that if you were a widow you would not have to stop reading this book in order to make dinner for your husband. And you are <u>appalled</u> at the direction your thoughts have taken, of course you don’t wish death upon your spouse, but you can’t help wishing he could just magically disappear for the next couple of days? And you push those demon thoughts aside, dutifully make dinner, gulp it down, do those damn dishes, and race back to your book. And that’s when your husband decides that NOW he wants to talk to you, and you think that maybe your earlier thoughts had not really been all that harsh?<br><br>That was how this book made me feel. This was hands-down one of the most entertaining books I have ever read. Maybe it was a case of the right book at the right time, but I loved every word of it and am sorely disappointed that I am done with it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1389234630i/8008976._SX540_.jpg" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>NOTE: Honey, if you’re reading this review, just kidding... kinda sorta! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3385900354085299095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320344604" />
    <a title="Idarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah"><img alt="Idarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596863879p2/1283951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320344604?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Idarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Idarah" href="/user/show/1283951-idarah">Idarah</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906462024" href="/book/show/2277185.Miss_Pettigrew_Lives_for_a_Day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283951-idarah?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320344604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17387958537344529767"><a href='https://www.flickr.com/photos/150051160@N07/40097027685/in/dateposted-public/' title='fullsizeoutput_911' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521912560i/25268652.jpg' width='375' height='500' alt='fullsizeoutput_911' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>"She prayed desperately for a knock on the door. A knock on Miss LaFosse's door heralded adventure. It was not like an ordinary house, when the knocker would be the butcher, or baker or candlestick-maker. A knock on Miss LaFosse's door would mean excitement, drama, a new crisis to be dealt with."—Miss Pettigrew</b><br/><br/>Dear, Miss Pettigrew! A woman after my own heart! Practically on the steps of the workhouse, Miss Pettigrew can't imagine that her last ditch effort to secure a post as a governess wil</span>
  <span id="freeText17387958537344529767" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/150051160@N07/40097027685/in/dateposted-public/" title="fullsizeoutput_911" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521912560i/25268652.jpg" width="375" height="500" alt="fullsizeoutput_911" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>"She prayed desperately for a knock on the door. A knock on Miss LaFosse's door heralded adventure. It was not like an ordinary house, when the knocker would be the butcher, or baker or candlestick-maker. A knock on Miss LaFosse's door would mean excitement, drama, a new crisis to be dealt with."—Miss Pettigrew</b><br><br>Dear, Miss Pettigrew! A woman after my own heart! Practically on the steps of the workhouse, Miss Pettigrew can't imagine that her last ditch effort to secure a post as a governess will lead to a twenty-four hour day of glamour, excitement and the way the other half (or sinners, as her vicar would say) live. I remember not being a fan of the film when I saw it years ago, but was determined to give the book a try regardless. So glad I did! Maybe I wasn't ready for Miss Pettigrew's charms, or the thrills of London circa 1938. I've been chastened. There is so much to learn! For example:<br><br><b>"Our Vicar once said that to swear in your mind was just as bad and even more cowardly than to swear out loud. He did neither."</b><br><br>What about makeup?<br><br><b>"All these years and she had never had the wicked thrill of powdering her nose...And all because she lacked courage. All because she had never thought for herself. Powder, thundered her father the curate, the road to damnation. Lipstick, whispered her mother, the first step on the downward path. Rouge, fulminated her father, the harlot's enticement. Eyebrow pencil, breathed her mother, no lady...!"</b><br><br>Silky drawers?<br><br><b>"'But the young girls!' Miss Pettigrew shook her head. 'Silk it is and silk it has to be. No warmth at all. I don't know how they don't all die of pneumonia. You cannot make them understand that they look <i>better</i> for wool. A warm body means a glowing face. A cold body means a pinched look and a red nose.'"</b><br><br>I'm sure that I'll be coming round to this one quite frequently, just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/683264.The_Diary_of_a_Provincial_Lady" title="The Diary of a Provincial Lady by E.M. Delafield" rel="nofollow noopener">The Diary of a Provincial Lady</a>. Highly recommend!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17387958537344529767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14865005949660609938" style="display:none">What a lovely story! I really enjoyed this book, and read it in a couple of days. I'm really glad Persephone books saved this book and brought back to life.<br />I can imagine it being a hit back at the times it was printed. It's a very lovely feminist story with a lead character, Miss Pettigrew. <br />The story takes place all in one day, which is another interesting aspect of this book. It actually reminded me of a theatre play. It was very dynamic, dramatic and energetic. <br />In addition, it was very uplifting. So, if you're looking for a lovely story that will warm your heart. It's definitely recommended. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1991487283" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1991487283?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11768149-miss-pettigrew-lives-for-a-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=tbr-2019">tbr-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1991487283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16203104816956522573">For the most part*, this is a delightful little book full of life and the joys of the fast life in pre-war England when it was first published (1938). <br/><br/>Miss Guinevere Pettigrew, a timid and down-trodden middle-aged spinster, has recently lost her job as a governess and in her search for a new position her employment agency gives her the wrong address for an interview. Instead of a family with young children she finds the door being opened by Miss Delysia LaFosse, a beautiful actress and night clu</span>
  <span id="freeText16203104816956522573" style="display:none">For the most part*, this is a delightful little book full of life and the joys of the fast life in pre-war England when it was first published (1938). <br /><br />Miss Guinevere Pettigrew, a timid and down-trodden middle-aged spinster, has recently lost her job as a governess and in her search for a new position her employment agency gives her the wrong address for an interview. Instead of a family with young children she finds the door being opened by Miss Delysia LaFosse, a beautiful actress and night club singer with an astounding number of men chasing after her. With her ability to read people and her good old common sense, Miss Pettigrew is able to advise Delysia on how to deal with her man problems and in return enjoys a day full of glamour and delights totally unknown to her before now. At the end of the day both Miss Pettigrew and Miss LaFosse will have been transformed in ways they didn't think possible.<br /><br />___________________________________<br /><br />*Just noting that there were a few occasions where mysogynist or anti-semitic comments made me gasp before reminding myself that this book was written in an earlier age, in the period between the wars when these sentiments would not have been thought wrong, and before much needed sweeping changes would be made to society. For example:<br /><br />From a man who wants to marry Miss LaFosse:<br /><i>"Now Delysia's a little devil and there's times I could flay her alive, and obviously she needs a little physical correction, but I'm the only right man to do it."</i><br /><br />Miss Pettigrew's comments about one of Miss LaFosse's suitors:<br /><i>"I wouldn't advise marrying him. I don't like to jump to conclusions but I think there was a little Jew in him. He wasn't quite English. And, well, I do think when it comes to marriage it's safer to stick with your own nationality."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16203104816956522573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16948316238539260908">I was supposed to be doing homework, but I chose to spend an hour finishing Miss Pettigrew instead. I regret nothing. <br/>The book is charming, and so is the movie. See and read both versions for full appreciation - read the book because it's fun, silly, and just a nice read overall. This was chick lit before chick lit was even a real genre. If that makes sense at all. See the movie because Frances McDormand is Miss Pettigrew, and it is perfect.   <span id="freeText16948316238539260908" style="display:none">I was supposed to be doing homework, but I chose to spend an hour finishing Miss Pettigrew instead. I regret nothing. <br />The book is charming, and so is the movie. See and read both versions for full appreciation - read the book because it's fun, silly, and just a nice read overall. This was chick lit before chick lit was even a real genre. If that makes sense at all. See the movie because Frances McDormand is Miss Pettigrew, and it is perfect. The film also features Lee Pace, aka Clive Owen's Hotter Long-Lost Twin. You thought it wasn't possible, but I assure you, it is.<br />Ahem. Anyway. Here, have an excerpt: <br />" 'That's cocaine,' said Miss LaFosse. <br />'Oh no! No!' <br />Terrified, aghast, thrilled, Miss Pettigrew stared at the innocent-looking powder. Drugs, the White Slave Traffic, wicked dives of iniquity, typified in Miss Pettigrew's mind by red plush and gilt and men with sinister black moustaches, roamed in wild array through her mind. What dangerous den of vice had she discovered? She must fly before she lost her virtue. Then her common sense unhappily reminded her that no one, now, would care to deprive her of that possession. It was Miss LaFosse who was in danger. She must save her. She jumped to her feet, tore into the kitchen, and scattered the powder down the sink and returned triumphant. <br />'There!' she said breathlessly. 'That bit of temptation is beyond your reach now.' "</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10622439739799887646">Sheer, light-hearted, sparkling fun.<br/><br/> Due to a mix up at her employment agency, Miss Pettigrew, a dowdy spinster looking for a position as a governess is sent to the address of an actress and nightclub singer, Miss Lafosse. Miss Lafosse is beautiful, glamorous and a little bit fast. Not a lady, and not the sort Miss Pettigrew has been brought up to associate herself with. she is however friendly, nice and in need of a bit of help to sort out her tangled love-life. Miss Pettigrew decides to give h</span>
  <span id="freeText10622439739799887646" style="display:none">Sheer, light-hearted, sparkling fun.<br /><br /> Due to a mix up at her employment agency, Miss Pettigrew, a dowdy spinster looking for a position as a governess is sent to the address of an actress and nightclub singer, Miss Lafosse. Miss Lafosse is beautiful, glamorous and a little bit fast. Not a lady, and not the sort Miss Pettigrew has been brought up to associate herself with. she is however friendly, nice and in need of a bit of help to sort out her tangled love-life. Miss Pettigrew decides to give herself over and enjoy a day that includes beauty treatments, cocktail parties and nightclubs with her new friends, and not worry about being a respectable 'lady'. A modern(ish) day fairy tale to warm the heart. I loved the simple illustrations that accompanied the story.</span>

    <a title="·Karen·" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1652898-karen"><img alt="·Karen·" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434742215p2/1652898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1329039387?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="·Karen·" class="user" itemprop="url" name="·Karen·" href="/user/show/1652898-karen">·Karen·</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906462024" href="/book/show/2277185.Miss_Pettigrew_Lives_for_a_Day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1652898-karen?shelf=brits">brits</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1652898-karen?shelf=f2f-book-group-reads">f2f-book-group-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1329039387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7719088820174922428">A fairy tale for the faint-hearted.<br/><br/>The <i>charming</i> story of how young Winnie came to write a book claims that her first job didn't exactly tax her time, so she filled her empty work hours with novels. One of her sisters asked what she was reading, to which she replied that it was awful nonsense and she could do better herself; her brother-in-law told her to get on with it, then. Apparently she wrote the whole of her first novel in the mornings at work. (Where do such jobs still exist? I'll put in m</span>
  <span id="freeText7719088820174922428" style="display:none">A fairy tale for the faint-hearted.<br /><br />The <i>charming</i> story of how young Winnie came to write a book claims that her first job didn't exactly tax her time, so she filled her empty work hours with novels. One of her sisters asked what she was reading, to which she replied that it was awful nonsense and she could do better herself; her brother-in-law told her to get on with it, then. Apparently she wrote the whole of her first novel in the mornings at work. (Where do such jobs still exist? I'll put in my visa application tomorrow.)<br /><br />I'm touched by his confidence in her abilities, but I do wish he'd directed her to better reading instead. <br /><br />Now, this is invariably called <i>charming</i>, but I am wearing my charm resistant suit today. I found it more weirdly disturbing to think that such a grotesque world may well have existed, where a man proves his manliness by socking another on the nose, and this is considered to be restoring the natural order, since the 'manly' socker was a fine upstanding Englishman and the other nothing but a wimpy foreigner, by Jove, and as such was bound not to put up a fight. And the worst misdemeanour a woman can commit is having a shiny nose.<br /><br />Didn't ever make me laugh either. Dear me, charm-safe suit <i>and</i> humour bypass, both on the same day. Must be hormonal.<br /><br />It <b>is</b> a fairy tale, of course it is, and thus not to be taken seriously. And like all good fairy tales, it has a moral: only drink enough Manhattans or Snake's Venoms or Death in the Afternoons and you can shake off all social awkwardness and say anything to anyone, and what's more they will find you <i>charming</i>. Sounds like a recipe for a fun weekend. Where's the vodka?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7719088820174922428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1729537834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1729537834" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1729537834?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906462024" href="/book/show/2277185.Miss_Pettigrew_Lives_for_a_Day">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729537834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17926011188068777764">This is the story of Miss Pettigrew, a 40-year-old woman who until now has lived a very innocent, troublefree and rather boring life. However, as the title of this novel indicates, we get to follow Miss Pettigrew on a special day when she encounters enough adventures to last her for a lifetime. These adventures change her, and while we read about her day we also learn about her as a person: both who she was before and who she's becoming now. <br/>A lot of Miss Pettigrew's adventures were very enterta</span>
  <span id="freeText17926011188068777764" style="display:none">This is the story of Miss Pettigrew, a 40-year-old woman who until now has lived a very innocent, troublefree and rather boring life. However, as the title of this novel indicates, we get to follow Miss Pettigrew on a special day when she encounters enough adventures to last her for a lifetime. These adventures change her, and while we read about her day we also learn about her as a person: both who she was before and who she's becoming now. <br />A lot of Miss Pettigrew's adventures were very entertaining to read about, and I liked how this book deals with how everyone has a different side inside of them. You might know who you are, but you can easily change if circumstances require it. <br />It was very easy to like Miss Pettigrew, and while some of her behaviour and her adventures were a little bit exaggerated, it was still very entertaining to follow her day from hour to hour and change together with her. All in all, a funny, rather educating read that I recommend if you need a short story that will take you on quite a thought-provoking journey. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17926011188068777764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2365530476" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365530476" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2365530476?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906462024" href="/book/show/2277185.Miss_Pettigrew_Lives_for_a_Day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=z-1001-books">z-1001-books</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=2020-reading-list">2020-reading-list</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=i-need-dis">i-need-dis</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=dws-birthday-challenge">dws-birthday-challenge</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2365530476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17237946901202567819">I felt a certain kinship with Miss Pettigrew—although considerably younger when I arrived in the big city, I was an unsophisticated farm girl, green as grass, totally out of my element and doubting whether I would ever attain the confidence that many of my peers demonstrated. I had a roommate who took me in hand and got me herded in the right direction, just as Miss Le Fosse and Miss DuBarry do for Guinevere Pettigrew.<br/><br/>However, Miss P has been a governess for many years and has taken care of hers</span>
  <span id="freeText17237946901202567819" style="display:none">I felt a certain kinship with Miss Pettigrew—although considerably younger when I arrived in the big city, I was an unsophisticated farm girl, green as grass, totally out of my element and doubting whether I would ever attain the confidence that many of my peers demonstrated. I had a roommate who took me in hand and got me herded in the right direction, just as Miss Le Fosse and Miss DuBarry do for Guinevere Pettigrew.<br /><br />However, Miss P has been a governess for many years and has taken care of herself during that time. She has what we now call transferable skills. She can cook an unexpected breakfast, find a way to heave a man out the door, convince the next fellow that those cheroots were hers, and manage a pouting young man back to his fiancée. And she is absolutely masterful at any of these tasks once she has a bit of alcohol in her. It overcomes her hesitations and self-doubts and allows her inner extremely competent governess out to deal with things. If you can run a classroom of small children, manipulating adults (who have ideas of social niceties) is easy, if you have the aplomb to carry it off. Frankly, a tot of something before facing the children would likely have made her into a better governess.<br /><br />There is much to be said for being ladylike, but if it isn't working for you, letting go of it is the right move. Learning to dress, wear make-up, hold her liquor, and make conversation…that's a lot to absorb in a day. That tells me that Miss P is an intelligent, adaptable woman who has been denied advantages by the polite class. It's the not-so-polite-society folks who see her worth and her talent. Her inexperience shows and amuses them, but they don't hold it against her, in fact they encourage her, mentor her. <br /><br />I found myself moved by the kindness of these people who had only known Guinevere for less than a day. And I loved Joe. I think that Watson stopped the novel at the perfect spot, where the potential for happiness is clear but we don't need to dwell on the detail. What a charming story!<br /><br />Cross posted at my blog:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://wanda-thenextfifty.blogspot.com/2020/10/miss-pettigrew-lives-for-day-winifred.html">https://wanda-thenextfifty.blogspot.c...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17237946901202567819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10559132214559900313"><b>Rating Clarification: 3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>This is a seriously old fashioned and charming adult fairy tale, and I mean that in the best way. Reading it is much like being transported into one of those classic black and white comedies starring Myrna Loy or Cary Grant; very stylish, slapdash and engaging, but with little substance. I feel that the recent movie adaptation added that much needed substance perfectly, which is why I'll classify the book version of <i>Miss Pettigrew Lives for a Day</i> much like I do for</span>
  <span id="freeText10559132214559900313" style="display:none"><b>Rating Clarification: 3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />This is a seriously old fashioned and charming adult fairy tale, and I mean that in the best way. Reading it is much like being transported into one of those classic black and white comedies starring Myrna Loy or Cary Grant; very stylish, slapdash and engaging, but with little substance. I feel that the recent movie adaptation added that much needed substance perfectly, which is why I'll classify the book version of <i>Miss Pettigrew Lives for a Day</i> much like I do for the book, <i>The Ghost and Mrs. Muir</i>:<br /><b>decent book, better movie adaptation</b>.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />(Extra brownie points for the Persephone Classics edition, which features the original 1930's drawings throughout the book - very cute).<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2258508089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2258508089" />
    <a title="Linda Dobinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32368211-linda-dobinson"><img alt="Linda Dobinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403100778p2/32368211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2258508089?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda Dobinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda Dobinson" href="/user/show/32368211-linda-dobinson">Linda Dobinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906462024" href="/book/show/2277185.Miss_Pettigrew_Lives_for_a_Day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32368211-linda-dobinson?shelf=favourite-classics">favourite-classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32368211-linda-dobinson?shelf=modern-classics">modern-classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2258508089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4783495992428229673">Miss Pettigrew Lives for a Day is a delightful story that is very much of its day. I absolutely loved it.<br/>It can be described as a Cinderella story though Delysia LaFosse and Edythe Dubarry are reversals of the ugly sisters.<br/>As the title suggests the action takes place over the course of one day. Each chapter covers a few hours so the pace is fast.<br/>Guinevere Pettigrew is a forty year old spinster who had led a drab, malnourished existence as a not-very-good governess. Terrorised by employers and ch</span>
  <span id="freeText4783495992428229673" style="display:none">Miss Pettigrew Lives for a Day is a delightful story that is very much of its day. I absolutely loved it.<br />It can be described as a Cinderella story though Delysia LaFosse and Edythe Dubarry are reversals of the ugly sisters.<br />As the title suggests the action takes place over the course of one day. Each chapter covers a few hours so the pace is fast.<br />Guinevere Pettigrew is a forty year old spinster who had led a drab, malnourished existence as a not-very-good governess. Terrorised by employers and charges alike she is now on the threshold of destitution. The one bright spot in her life is her ''weekly orgy at the cinema'' (p3).<br />When she arrives at 5, Onslow Mansions to apply for yet another dismal position she is shocked when the woman who answers the door is not a bad tempered matron but a ''creature...so lovely she called to mind immediately the beauties of the screen'' (p3).<br />Miss Pettigrew has two sides to her character. The prim and proper moral side that comes from being the daughter of a curate who thought make-up was the ''road to damnation'' (p73), and a repressed fun, naughty side that likes movies her parents would have disapproved of. As she enters Miss LaFosse's flat these two side battle as she notes the pictures on the walls are ''not quite decent'' (p4), yet she feels ''a strange kind of excitement'' (P5).<br />Unlike the people she has come across all her life, Delysia and her friend Edythe treat Miss Pettigrew kindly and as an equal. So do their lovers by not subjecting her to the ''polite, excluding courtesies that had been her measure from men all her life '' (9).<br />As the day develops so does Miss Pettigrew's fun side as she abandons many of her former beliefs and gives herself up wholeheartedly to her new friends who appreciate her worth.<br />I recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4783495992428229673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3421090373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3421090373" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2967061-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577653837p2/2967061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9310893962014700826">A charming, and uplifting adult fairy tale wonderfully narrated by Frances McDormand. Two women diametrically opposed in all ways such wealth and class, character (unworldly) and many meet by accident and spend 24 hours together in a fun plot with well-drawn characters. By story's end, each one has had a major influence on the life and future of the other. Miss Pettigrew steals the show; she is such a wonderful character and watching her reactions as she is introduced to new experiences througho</span>
  <span id="freeText9310893962014700826" style="display:none">A charming, and uplifting adult fairy tale wonderfully narrated by Frances McDormand. Two women diametrically opposed in all ways such wealth and class, character (unworldly) and many meet by accident and spend 24 hours together in a fun plot with well-drawn characters. By story's end, each one has had a major influence on the life and future of the other. Miss Pettigrew steals the show; she is such a wonderful character and watching her reactions as she is introduced to new experiences throughout the novel is both touching and fun to behold. The way her life changes at the end is very poignant and ends the story perhaps predictably but no matter, it put a big smile on my face. <br /><br />Published by Persephone Press.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393450215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16432797722757862236">I hesitated over giving this book five stars. "It's fluff," I told myself. "This is not a Literary Masterpiece. It's a fun novel. It's frivolous. How can I give something so frivolous five stars?" I summed up the plot in my head to see if some Serious, Important aspect of the novel had slipped past my notice. It hadn't. The book was exactly as promised (in some review, somewhere, I'll find it later): a champagne comedy. Sweet, bubbly, light.<br/><br/>It was then that I recalled a similar description had b</span>
  <span id="freeText16432797722757862236" style="display:none">I hesitated over giving this book five stars. "It's fluff," I told myself. "This is not a Literary Masterpiece. It's a fun novel. It's frivolous. How can I give something so frivolous five stars?" I summed up the plot in my head to see if some Serious, Important aspect of the novel had slipped past my notice. It hadn't. The book was exactly as promised (in some review, somewhere, I'll find it later): a champagne comedy. Sweet, bubbly, light.<br /><br />It was then that I recalled a similar description had been applied to Pride and Prejudice. A novel about a houseful of daughters, trying to get married. Sparkling, funny, but it isn't exactly Serious Ponderings either.<br /><br />Then I remembered that Miss Pettigrew had made me laugh until I wheezed on a public train. (Several times.) I essentially read it in two sittings. I couldn't wait to get back to it, to see what happened next. I will definitely be keeping it. It made me extoll the virtues of both book and movie to a friend, so much so that we're having a movie night next week.<br /><br />When was the last time a book had done that for me? Last year? The year before?<br /><br />If Pride and Prejudice can be a five star novel, so can this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16432797722757862236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer515799101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7314615942785944732">This is such a delightful read, I loved it from beginning to end! I've been reading so many books lately that I wished would have been shorter but with Miss Pettigrew I wish the book would have been much longer:) <br/><br/>I can't believe I came across this charming, beguiling, uplifting, feel good tale by pure chance, it must have been my lucky day! This became an instant classic to me after the first few pages. I just love Watson's writing, the way she portrays the characters and their feelings. Miss Pe</span>
  <span id="freeText7314615942785944732" style="display:none">This is such a delightful read, I loved it from beginning to end! I've been reading so many books lately that I wished would have been shorter but with Miss Pettigrew I wish the book would have been much longer:) <br /><br />I can't believe I came across this charming, beguiling, uplifting, feel good tale by pure chance, it must have been my lucky day! This became an instant classic to me after the first few pages. I just love Watson's writing, the way she portrays the characters and their feelings. Miss Pettigrew really is a gem and such a refreshing read! It has been such a long time since I last felt so excited about a book and it's such a fantastic feeling!<br /><br />I'm aware that this review doesn't make much sense and isn't very constructive but this books is simply great so there isn't much more to say about it:)</span>

    <a title="Luce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1214888-luce"><img alt="Luce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566854740p2/1214888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2157119627?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luce" href="/user/show/1214888-luce">Luce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/26749375-miss-pettigrew-lives-for-a-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1214888-luce?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1214888-luce?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1214888-luce?shelf=location-outside-us">location-outside-us</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1214888-luce?shelf=job-actor-dancer">job-actor-dancer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1214888-luce?shelf=job-maid-housekeeper-nanny">job-maid-housekeeper-nanny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1214888-luce?shelf=job-personal-assistant">job-personal-assistant</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2157119627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4632825561581195190">4 Stars for the book, 5th star for the narrator, Frances McDormand)<br/><br/>A fun book written in 1938, that takes place in London and is the basis of the 2008 film with Frances McDormand as Miss Pettigrew and Amy Adams as the nightclub singer, Delysia Lafosse. LaFosse was an American in the film. Pettigrew, a 40 yr old spinster who until now lived a sheltered and uneventful life. She is an out of work governess who is sent to Delysia's for a job. Pettigrew is caught in the whirlwind of the glamorous, De</span>
  <span id="freeText4632825561581195190" style="display:none">4 Stars for the book, 5th star for the narrator, Frances McDormand)<br /><br />A fun book written in 1938, that takes place in London and is the basis of the 2008 film with Frances McDormand as Miss Pettigrew and Amy Adams as the nightclub singer, Delysia Lafosse. LaFosse was an American in the film. Pettigrew, a 40 yr old spinster who until now lived a sheltered and uneventful life. She is an out of work governess who is sent to Delysia's for a job. Pettigrew is caught in the whirlwind of the glamorous, Delysia. Delysia befriends Pettigrew and takes her on an entertaining adventure. A day in the life of Delysia, so to speak. It is told from Pettigrew's POV and it is interesting to see how much she grows and changes in a day. We also see the effect Pettigrew has on Delysia. <br /><br />A fun book, with excellent narration by McDormand. At times she sounded quite like Amy Adams when voicing Delysia. As is often the case whenever you compare the book with the movie, I thought the book was much better but I will still enjoy watching the movie. When I watch a movie or read a book it was based on, I try to see them as separate entities. Otherwise you will surely be disappointed. I highly recommend the audiobook and the movie. Just be aware they different in many ways but just as fun. Or as one GR reviewer stated - the movie manages to catch and reflect the spirit of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4632825561581195190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f598gn/PIcGGrlepmbIx+Q0Dw+Q2uH2Mkb5zTNXWhptd+PSvS1V5YwqoHFvieMn7gXPN1w0jVrssmGM98Bodbg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('k6adYn/5HoUEnE2YP6+c5F5kt3OhL+Asc2Y38lp7q9CxwRVPS2NGJ4iaBmpEZWTm0hS5QJq0yxvOQCeDf7cwJQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
